She soon followed up with a critically acclaimed jazz-tinged album with a 90 word title...<BR>Yeah. this girl wasn't what we expected.<br />Tidal isn't what we expected. It manages to achieve more than the female grunge/pop. Lyrically and musically, this album rises above the two genres weaknesses and achieves something rarely heard...musical and lyrical individualism...a grating, painful musical concept if used inappropriately. Yet the content heard on Tidal is the very definition of how taking your own path and doing your own thing is the best and most original way.<br />The lyrics concern Fiona, her emotional problems, and her dealings with the Ego...not that this is philosophy class, but one guesses that Fiona probably likes Ayn Rand books. At least Fiona is honest about her self-absorption vs. the Sting, \\"save the animals\\" approach. If self-absorption isn't your thing and celebrity faux-altruism is, then maybe this isn't the album for you, and pick up one of those grating New York tribute albums, or Michael Jackson's \\"We Are the World\\" single instead. <br />None of Fiona's attitudes read literally. In fact, literally they read like an extended monologue to a lover explaining her various weaknesses as a person and her need to repair those weaknesses. But instead of simple self-pity, Fiona also has some swagger, some kick, and self-confidence that prevales occasionally from the doom and gloom. For all Fiona complains about how little of a person she is, she really does have a healthy sense of herself. <br />\\"And you'll yield to me, like a scent in the breeze\\" she slurs in Slow Like Honey, obviously aware of the power she holds over men. <br />The songwriting is sophisticated and jazzy with a staying power that ranks it in the classics. I can say with full relish that 6 years later, \\"Criminal\\" is still one awesome tune...it's almost surprising that it was a hit, considering the low standard that radio consistently plays.  This album is chock full of amazing songs...I could go on and on about the virtues of each one. Andrew Slater's production accentuates the blues and soul prevalent in both her music and her emotions. <br />Unfortunately, the music industry never truly appreciated Fiona...they kept on painting that unfortunate Alanis Morrissette-esque grungy portrait, when really Fiona's songwriting and vocal styles recall nothing but herself. Remember this is individualism, pure and simple. <br />Tidal is a different album, unique and more than a bit odd. Yet it's aim is so exact and the aspirations Fiona has are so dead on, that it remains the most effective self-confessional singer-songwriter experiment in individualism the 90's and perhaps the entirety of musical has beared witness to.
B00006F7XJ|3.0|This is not a particularly energetic effort. Where many of the songs contain interesting passages, overall, there is an absence of strong compositions. It's a shame as it leaves the listener, and long time fan, somewhat disapointed. Still it's nice to know that even if the old farts are slowing down, along with the meter, they are still around making an honest effort. Perhaps Latimer could take a page out Ian Anderson's book and upgrade the band in order to rejuvenate it and keep it vital and energetic. Proceed with caution...Simon

0789420694|4.0|Robert Louis Stevenson's \\"Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde\\" is one of the classics of horror literature because it provides the paradigmatic example of the \\"werewolf,\\" the human being with a monstrous alter ego.  However, originally it was much more of a mystery story and that is the best way of describing this adaptation of Stevenson's novella by Michael Lawrence.  The book's complex structure is simplified and Lawrence employs a narrator to help retell the tale.  The adaptation is certainly competent enough, but the story clearly takes a back seat to the illustrations in this particular volume.<br />This Eyewitness Classics adaptation of \\"Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde\\" is full of the illustrations and details we have come to associate with books put out by DK Publishing.  A two-page spread before the first chapter details The Two Face of London, contrasting the rich West End of Victorian London with Soho area where criminals stalked the poor.  Background about how Victorian gentlemen dressed for evening and how women were second-class citizens is provided.  Once the story commences there are not only illustrations by Ian Andrew depicting events in the novella, but the borders are usually filled with small photographs and detailed text amplifying the action.  One such note might explaining the gas lighting system in use at the time while another actually explains the significance of the key Jekyll supposedly gave to Hyde.  These pictures and notes are certainly informative, but they are also somewhat intrusive, especially when the reader is trying to decide when they should read each of these additional bits of information.<br />The attempt here is to provide something more than a straightforward presentation of the novella without going so far as to provide an annotated version.  The information provided is quite useful for young readers, for the most part, but their intrusiveness may well get in the way of enjoying the story itself.  The illustrations by Andrew are stylistically evocative of the shadowy, misty streets of London we associate with tales of violent crimes such as \\"Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde.\\"  A final spread in the back of the book looks at the Legend of the story, which includes the various dramatic versions on stage and screen.  More interesting are the insights into how the story reflected what people were thinking about evolution, psychology, and drugs at the end of the 19th-century.  The best solution might be to just try and read the story without always resorting to the additional information and then going back and filling in the details (maybe on a chapter by chapter basis).  This approach is used in a pair of other \\"horror\\" classics, \\"Dracula\\" and \\"The Hunchback of Notre Dame,\\" in the DK Classics series.ally evocative of the shadowy, misty streets of London we associate with tales of violent crimes such as \\"Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde.\\"  A final spread in the back of the book looks at the Legend of the story, which includes the various dramatic versions on stage and screen. B00001ZULV|4.0|As the title, &quot;Turn It On Again: The Hits&quot; suggests, this Genesis compilation simply represents the band's *hits* (well, most of them). This is not a &quot;Best-Of&quot; retrospective of the band's career, just the stuff that made it onto the singles charts, which explains why the lion's share of this album comes from the Phil Collins era, Peter Gabriel's era is only represented twice, and Ray Wilson only once. Still, as a longtime Genesis follower, I'm very pleased with this disc, as it represents a great time when these guys were a strong presence on the radio airwaves. If you're a Genesis fan, either diehard or just casual, then listening to this CD will be a nice stroll down memory lane.Most of the usual suspects are here: &quot;Follow You Follow Me,&quot; &quot;Abacab&quot; (single version), &quot;That's All,&quot; &quot;Invisible Touch,&quot; &quot;Tonight Tonight Tonight&quot; (single version), &quot;No Son Of Mine,&quot; and &quot;I Can't Dance.&quot; Thankfully, Ray Wilson's brief time as the group's frontman is represented here by &quot;Congo,&quot; which briefly charted in the UK (I'm glad that at least *one* track from the very-overlooked Genesis album, &quot;Calling All Stations,&quot; will be heard by somebody). And Peter Gabriel's only &quot;hits&quot; with the band, &quot;I Know What I Like&quot; &amp; &quot;The Carpet Crawlers&quot; (both charted in the UK), are also here. And speaking of &quot;The Carpet Crawlers,&quot; this version is a remake, with Gabriel, Collins, and guitarist Steve Hackett briefly returning to the fold for a handsome 1999 reworking of this classic nugget from &quot;The Lamb Lies Down On Broadway&quot; (though everybody in the band recorded their parts separately). Quite possibly the very last thing the band will ever record together, this '99 &quot;Carpet Crawlers,&quot; like the original version, is a sheer beauty. The album is worth getting just for this one track alone.    However, with only so much space to workwith on a compact disc, several other chart singles by Genesis have been left off, such as &quot;Ripples,&quot; &quot;Your Own Special Way,&quot; &quot;No Reply At All,&quot; &quot;Man On The Corner,&quot; &quot;Paperlate,&quot; and &quot;Never A Time.&quot; Still, all things considered, &quot;Turn It On Again: The Hits&quot; is a very good representation of Genesis' most popular tunes. And if you're simply a casual fan, well then, get it for the hits. Either way, it's a win-win purchase. :-)

B000002UB3|5.0|If I had to choose which record by the Beatles, one of my favorite groups ever, I enjoyed the most, I would think for a few seconds, debate between The White Album and Abbey Road, and then choose the latter. It may have been the last recording they ever made, but they made much use of what little time they had left.<br />Abbey Road kicks off with &quot;Come Together&quot;, which is probably the best track on side one. It's a pretty subdued track until the end, but John's surreal lyrics are as good as they're ever going to get here. &quot;Maxwell's Silver Hammer&quot; is Paul's demented tale about a serial killer, which manages to work on many levels. Rounding off side one is the bizarre &quot;I Want You (She's So Heavy)&quot;; after switching back and forth between varying tempos for four minutes, the group finally decides on one, and continues playing it for the last three minutes, while white noise slowly engulfs the song.<br />Side two, however, is how the Beatles left their legacy to the world. &quot;Here Comes the Sun&quot; is a very uplifting song, written by none other than George Harrison. &quot;Because&quot; has some of the most gorgeous melodies ever recorded.<br />After this, the first of the two famous medleys begins with &quot;You Never Give Me Your Money&quot;, which is the most accomplished song of the 5-song medley. It segues into the beautiful &quot;Sun King&quot;, written and sung by John. After this is the psychadelic &quot;Mean Mr. Mustard&quot;, a great, albeit short, number.<br />Before I continue, I would just like to make a short note. &quot;Her Majesty&quot;, which is at the end of Abbey Road, was actually meant to go right after &quot;Mean Mr. Mustard&quot;. Paul didn't like it, however, so he had the song cut out of the medley. However, it was accidentally put at the end of the master tape, but the Beatles liked it, so they kept it. I have used Cool Edit Pro to reinsert the song in between &quot;Mustard&quot; and &quot;Pam&quot;, and it sounds much more natural, in my opinion; it allows for a short, but needed, instrumental break in the medley. <br />Next is &quot;Polythene Pam&quot;, which flows right into &quot;She Came in Through the Bathroom Window&quot;, which is a great way to end the awesome first medley.<br />The second medley, though only three songs, is the best part of Abbey Road. It starts off with the touching &quot;Golden Slumbers&quot;, which then moves into &quot;Carry That Weight&quot;, which is sort of a reprise of &quot;YNGMYM&quot;, but features one of the greatest uses of a brass instrument in any song. Abbey Road ends with a song that is fitting called &quot;The End&quot;, which features the greatest line the Beatles ever sung in a song of theirs. If you don't know what it is, I won't tell you; it's probably best if you just listen to it yourself.<br />If you call yourself a Beatles fan, but haven't listened to Abbey Road, you're a liar. The Beatles were arguably the greatest rock band ever, and this album shows why.

Always, he yearned for freedom for his people from British rule.  And always, he preached non-violence.  It worked.  Eventually India did become independent. I love all those behind-the-scene stories, such as how he had to learn to spin fabric as part of his role and how difficult it was for him to spin and say his lines at the same time.  Also, in the funeral scene, which included 400,000 people, he actually played the part of the corpse instead of using a wax dummy.<br />I definitely recommend this DVD. B000055ZB8|5.0|1922 classic silent vampire film, the first of its kind, by German expressionists. Based on Dracula, this film deals with a man going to the \\"land of the phantoms\\" in Romania, to sell property, to a fellow, who turns out to be a vampire. The Vamp would like to kill his guest, but when he sees his wife, he travels to her town to have her. The scenes are brilliantly shot in black and white, in fearsome surroundings. Heavy shadows, and spooky music play. The camera is always still, it does not move. The acting or overacting is in the style of Expressionism, where all emotions are thrown out to be displayed. Before I sat down to watch this I felt a sense of dread, as I heard how great and terrifying this film is. As it started it got more and more eerier, and scary. I can understand why this film is regarded so high, as it is so entertaining, and captivating. That's quite good, since its in black and white with no sound, and moves at a slow pace. Seriously constructed by all who made this, I can see how it has survived and remained on critic's lists for 80 years, while modern horror films are forgotten after first viewing. Great addition to your library, 5 stars!

0375701427|5.0|Roth just seems  to get better and better. This is his finest work (along with Sabbath's theatre)--forget the magical realism and the embedded narrative. This book is a unforgiving but poignant meditation on the 60's--which had the patina of exhuberance but as Roth so deeply understands an underlying hurt, a pathology that  wrecked peoples lives--that caused damage that will take years--if ever to get over. I was a participant but I sensed it--the danger--in some inchoate way--at the time. It takes a great writer like Roth to articulate that dementia. Walker Percy sensed it also and wrote about it, but even his fine work (Lancelot for example) cannot match the subtlety the humor and the utter terror that Roth exposes. Be aware that Roth is not exxagerating--he is on the mark. The moral disintegration and the sanctimonious (and just plain old) violence really happened. The book is not a political tract--I am just focusng on that, but he details the period with the precision  of  an historian. He understands the \\"mere anarchy\\" that was the real agenda of the times.<BR>I omit his brilliant language and literary crafsmanship--his understanding of wounded human spirits because that should be obvious. <BR>He is the greatest writer of our times.

A great opener, and the first chord of roaring distortion sets the tone for the whole record. Rating: A <BR><BR>\\"Scenless Apprentice\\" contains some of the most primal screams, and the most graphic lyrics of Cobain's entire career. Rating: A <BR><BR>\\"Heart Shaped Box\\" is probably the most perverse love song of all time (\\"I wish I could eat your cancer when you turn black\\") nonetheless one of the greatest rock songs of all time. Rating: A+ <BR><BR>\\"Rape Me\\" is the most controversial song on the record, which DOES NOT promote rape. Kurt said that it was about bieng raped and the concept of karma. He said \\"the song is like 'rape me and you'll go to jail and get it 3x worse.'\\" An excellent guitar riff. Rating: A+<BR><BR>\\"Frances Farmer...\\" is definitely about a turmoiled relationship. \\"I miss the comfort in being sad\\" is one of the best lines Kurt ever came up with. Rating: A+<BR><BR>\\"Dumb\\" is probably the sweetest song in Nirvana's catalogue. The cello and the tone of Kurt's voice is a tearjerker. Rating: A+ <BR><BR>\\"Very Ape\\" is an ode to Neanderthals. \\"I take pride as the king of illiterature.\\" Great songs, and realistic about the lives of some of the jocks that bullied people like Kurt in high school. Short (at less than 2 minutes) but great. Rating: A+ <BR><br />\\"Milk It\\" is angry and visceral, and rivals \\"Scentless Apprentice\\" is the heaviest and angriest song on the record. With lyrics like \\"Look on the bright side is suicide,\\" you can tell that Kurt was one angry person. Strangely prophetic too. Rating: A+ <BR><BR>\\"Pennyroyal Tea\\" is a relic dating back to the Nevermind sessions. Great song with a melodic sense. Rating: A<BR><BR>\\"Radio Friendly Unit Shifer\\" is a bunch of feedback and interesting imagery.. it's pretty cool. Rating: A-<BR><BR>\\"tourette's\\" is just 95 seconds of Kurt screaming about god knows what. Great to listen to when those moments of frustration just come at you like a tidal wave. Rating: A <BR><BR>\\"All Apologies\\" is a perfect way to end the album. A heartfelt song, but rather disturbing at the same time, because some of the lyrics do foreshadow Kurt's suicide. <BR><BR>I think it's Nirvana's best album, and also a heartbreaking album which makes it hard to listen to sometimes. Nirvana definitely ended their album cycle with some great music.

An interesting concept album marking both the poignancies and idiocies of modern culture, \\"Vitalogy\\" really breathes in listening from start to finish.<br />The new directions and styles experimented with by the band on this record have been unfairly criticized by some Pearl Jam fans.  After all, how can a band creatively progress without such experimentation?  (Case in point, Radiohead's \\"OK Computer\\")  Though \\"Vs.\\" was a great album - and another one of the band's high points - one more guitar-anchored album and Pearl Jam might have drilled themselves into a hole.  And they knew it.  Songs such as \\"Bugs\\", a suprisingly humorous slant from an otherwise melodramatic group, and \\"Aye Davanita\\", a sweetly eastern-flavored hymn, were a breath of fresh air in the dingy corners of grunge in the mid-90s.  \\"Hey Sexymophandlemomma\\" is a track like no other; a seemingly inspired homage to the Beatles' \\"Revolution 9\\" (a sharp revolution that has yet to catch on).  These new directions for Pearl Jam, along with \\"Vitalogy's\\" acompanying eerie booklet, are what set them apart from other voiceless grunge bands of their time.  <br />What also stands out about this record is fact that the properly crafted songs on \\"Vitalogy\\" are some of the band's best.  \\"Corduroy\\", \\"Better Man\\", \\"Nothingman\\" and \\"Immortality\\" are golden.  Beautiful lyrics and melodies combined with interesting chord progressions and guitar licks abound.  The primary phrasing of \\"Tremors Christ\\" seems elementary, yet is simultaneously complex.  Repetitiveness gives way to dynamic in \\"Not For You\\".  And \\"Spin the Black Circle\\" is just flat-out rock n' roll fun.<br />\\"Vitalogy's\\" one and only downfall is the lull in it's middle.  Though \\"Whipping\\" - like almost any Pearl Jam song - blares solid lyrics and theme, it simply sounds awkward after the touching \\"Nothingman\\".  And though in \\"Pry, to\\" lies a point that Vedder yearns to get across, it really ends up as the throw-away transition to the record's second half.<br />Lyrical highlights include \\"Satan's Bed\\", \\"Not For You\\" and \\"Immortality\\".  Shining melodies grace almost every track on the album.  And there is the sense in each song that your are connecting with an important message.  (Even in \\"Bugs\\", which may or may not have social themes.)  The booklet alone could be the band's grandest statement, containing alarming past cultural morals and images.  From beginning to end, \\"Vitalogy\\" is Pearl Jam's greatest achievement, both musically and artistically.  If you didn't like it the first time, give it some time to grow on you.  Few rock albums of the 1990's will have as much vitalogy.

And each of these standout \\"leads\\" does a bloody good job of holding our interest till the end.<br /><br />I would certainly recommend this top-notch tongue-in-cheek murder mystery.

B00006DEFA|4.0|It is always very funny to see a Masterpiece made out of historical distortions.<br />I know that Peter Schaffer meant well by writing a play about the competition between Salieri and Mozart.<br />Unfortunately, history found Salieri far more successful in Austria and abroad than Mozart at that time.<br />Salieri was the \\"talk of the town\\", NOT Mozart...<br />So why is it that all of a sudden Salieri should become immensely jealous of Mozart and even go as far as to murder him for his music, if it should have been quite the opposite?<br />Schaffer needed a conflict situation in which to set his own Drama and add a scapegoat for the tragic death of the \\"brat\\".<br />This scapegoat happened to be Salieri.<br />Very good for someone who has never studied history of music, but what about historical accuracy? Goodbye and farewell...<br />Of all the enemies that Mozart made throughout his lifetime, Salieri should have been considered the less threatening of them all. He certainly didn't need it.<br />What about, instead, the many \\"close\\" friends, who flocked to Mozart's feasts/orgies?<br />Many of them were totally untalented musicians, eager to be \\"seen\\" with Mozart in order to even just be considered as such.<br />Couldn't one of them have had a secret wish to murder him, in order to steal his work and resell it for profit?<br />That would have been a true motivation for murder.<br />Instead we have a whimpering Salieri, who almost seems to be sexually attracted to the young Mozart and in a frenzy of jealousy, not only indirectly murders Mozart, by inciting him to \\"work harder\\" while the composer lies in bed feverish, but ultimately also attempts to committ suicide like a woman abandoned by her lover.<br />C'mon, not everybody is gay in this world! Let's get real for once.<br />Salieri who was Venetian by birth, exactly like Vivaldi, was a highly celebrated Court composer and beloved and envied for his position by everybody. Not only this, but he also had followers of his style throughout Europe.<br />Could a man like this really care about a newcomer like Mozart. Not really, especially because Mozart's music was only appreciated in France and in some remote corners of Germany. His popularity in those days was just limited by the fact, that he was an \\"Enfant prodige\\" and as such, more a Circus attraction than anything else.<br />His music was \\"tolerated\\" at best.<br interest in the composer's works and even then they didn't come through as masterpieces.<br />Beethoven was still far more popular in people's ears than Mozart.<br />Finally, and only after many following attempts by various parties to revive his music, did Amadeus' music make it in the \\"charts\\".<br />Almost a Century in fact, had past since the Maestro died and only now was his style truly admired and understood.<br />\\"Amadeus\\" is a totally fictionalized tale that may have some symbolism in it, but that's all it is.<br />I understand artistic licence to a point, but then my ethical instinct kicks in, and revulsion and rebellion sets in.<br />Like in \\"Immortal Beloved\\", a piece of [junk] unworthy of any true \\"follower\\" of Beethoven, this is totally unworthy of any true connaisseur of Master Mozart or even Master Salieri.<br />Hollywood will naturally praise its so-called \\"works of art\\", but only a completely illiterate [person] would agree with them.<br and totally unbelievable tale of two musicians who loved to hate each other (when would they ever have found the time to compose anything with so much mayhem?).<br />If instead, you are like me, a person with common sense and respect for \\"true\\" and well-written Biographies and History, then you will either take it as a purely \\"amazing stories\\" episode, a bit overstreched maybe, but watchable, or you will keep your fingers away of this one and go on listening directly to Mozart's or Salieri's music and make the necessary comparisons. B00004STW4|5.0|This film satisfies on so many levels. As about 100+ reviewers before me have commented, it's a really great spoof on those campy films of the 50's which I grew up on. However, it's also a truly magnificent social comment on how various strata of our society respond to crisis. Peace-freak types are ready to embrace the invaders, the academician assumes because they are technologically advanced, they come with benevolent intent and the governing bodies look to him for advice. The military types assume malevolent intent as a sort of knee-jerk reaction. The president assures the public \\"all is well' even though it isn't and tells them to go about their lives. The President and First Lady sit gulping their dinner(like the rest of us) while watching the glitzy newslady with the brain of an ambitious 6 year-old. The White House press secretary advises the Pres on various photo-ops. I could go on and on. This film is not only about 50's sci-fi flicks just as \\"Gulliver's Travels\\" was also not only a unique tale for children in its day. One only need to look at the current situation we find ourselves in with destructive forces from the Middle East to see the corresponding elements in this film. It not only satisfied the graying ex-English major in me but it is damn good fun. Brilliant but apparently misunderstood.
